### Generated Package

- **package_id:** d2ee2193-1340-4397-97bf-f9d3549573dd
- **title:** The Silent Social Media Tax Every Small Business Is Paying Without Realizing It
- **status:** draft
- **created_at:** 2026-07-01T21:16:47.19586+00:00
- **funnel_stage:** awareness

- **hook:** A potential customer just checked your profile — and left without a word.

**voiceover_text**

Someone Googled you, found your socials, and saw your last post was two months ago. They didn't DM you. They didn't complain. They just... left. No drama. No refund. You never even knew they were there. That's the silent tax — credibility lost one profile visit at a time. fenrik Studio turns your website into a month of ready-to-post content. First package is free.

**subtitles**

Someone Googled you. Found your socials. Last post: two months ago. They didn't complain. They just left. No drama. No refund. You never knew they were there. That's the silent tax — credibility lost one profile visit at a time. fenrik Studio turns your website into a month of ready-to-post content. First package is free.

- **scenario:** 

- **CTA type:** sign_up
- **CTA text:** Get your first content package free — just hand us your website URL, no payment needed.

**video concept**

A fast vertical short that opens on the eerie calm of a potential customer silently bouncing from a dormant social profile — no complaint, no signal, just gone. The unexpected turn: the business owner has no idea it happened. The punchline: the 'tax' was never on an invoice. The CTA lands the fix: one URL, a free first package. Mood is bright and dry-humorous, not dark — think wry observation, not horror.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — SITUATION (0–4s): Close-up of a phone screen showing a blurred social profile with a visible gap where recent posts should be. Voiceover: 'Someone Googled you, found your socials, and saw your last post was two months ago.' | BEAT 2 — UNEXPECTED TURN (4–12s): Cut to a cheerful business owner at their desk, totally unbothered, coffee in hand, completely unaware. Voiceover: 'They didn't DM you. They didn't complain. They just... left. No drama. No refund. You never even knew they were there.' | BEAT 3 — PUNCHLINE (12–18s): Graphic-style beat — a receipt visual with zero dollar amount but a bold label reading nothing legible, just abstract shapes suggesting a cost. Voiceover: 'That's the silent tax — credibility lost one profile visit at a time.' | BEAT 4 — CTA (18–23s): Clean bright frame, person types a URL into a simple form on a laptop with a blurred generic interface. Voiceover: 'fenrik Studio turns your website into a month of ready-to-post content. First package is free.'

- **duration_seconds:** 23

**image prompts**

1. Bright, clean close-up of a person's hand holding a modern smartphone, the screen showing a blurred social media profile page with a clearly visible empty section where recent posts would appear — soft natural daylight, white background, no readable text or UI labels anywhere on screen, abstract colorful blobs suggesting a dormant feed.
2. A cheerful small business owner sitting at a bright modern desk, coffee mug in hand, smiling and completely relaxed — warm natural light, tidy workspace, laptop open with a soft blurred colorful interface visible on screen, completely unaware of anything, upbeat and candid mood.
3. A stylized flat-lay of an abstract paper receipt on a clean white surface — the receipt is mostly blank with vague abstract shapes suggesting line items and a total, no readable numbers or words, a subtle visual metaphor for an invisible cost, bright daylight, minimal and graphic.
4. A person sitting at a bright modern desk, typing on a laptop with a soft blurred generic form interface glowing on the screen — clean white and neutral tones, open airy room, natural window light, calm and purposeful expression, no readable text on screen.

## Package 2 of 21

### Strategy Item

- **strategy_item_id:** ab04f876-3bce-4324-8dc6-083e69e26f24
- **package_index:** 1
- **topic:** Why the businesses you envy on social aren't working harder than you
- **angle:** Reframe the gap between high-output competitors and silent brands. It's not effort or creativity — it's a system. Introduce the idea that consistent content doesn't require a content team, it requires removing yourself from the production loop.
- **funnel_stage:** awareness
- **platform:** tiktok
- **format:** reel
- **priority:** 1
- **trend_id:** 
- **topic_id:** 
- **strategy_id:** 23efd70f-823b-475c-9839-7e959e0bd55e

### Generated Package

- **package_id:** 0477a7e6-f819-4d97-b8c2-67e3dd39fb1f
- **title:** Why the Businesses You Envy on Social Aren't Working Harder Than You
- **status:** draft
- **created_at:** 2026-07-01T21:17:30.842367+00:00
- **funnel_stage:** awareness

- **hook:** I'll admit it — I used to think those brands posting every single day had a whole team behind them. They don't.

**voiceover_text**

I used to think those brands posting every single day had a whole team behind them. They don't. The difference isn't effort — it's that they removed themselves from the production loop entirely. While you're juggling five platforms and a real business, they're not writing, filming, or editing anything. The content just runs. That's the system. And you can have it too.

**subtitles**

I used to think those brands posting every day had a whole team behind them. // They don't. // The difference isn't effort. // They removed themselves from the production loop. // While you're juggling five platforms and a real business — // they're not writing, filming, or editing anything. // The content just runs. // That's the system. // And you can have it too.

- **scenario:** 

- **CTA type:** sign_up
- **CTA text:** Hand us your website URL. Your first content package is free — no payment required.

**video concept**

A fast-paced vertical short that opens with a candid confession — the narrator assumed high-output brands had large teams. The visual journey moves from a frantic founder scrambling across multiple device screens, to a calm competitor brand whose content flows effortlessly, to the reveal: it's not manpower, it's a system that removes the human bottleneck entirely. The final beat is a clean, bright call to action. Tone is calm, authoritative, slightly conspiratorial — like a secret being shared, not sold.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — CONFESSION (0–4s): Close-up of a person glancing at a competitor's social feed, slightly wide-eyed. VO: 'I used to think those brands posting every single day had a whole team behind them.'

BEAT 2 — OBSERVATION (4–9s): Quick cuts — same person switching between phone, laptop, tablet, looking overwhelmed managing multiple platforms. VO: 'They don't. The difference isn't effort.'

BEAT 3 — MEANING (9–15s): Cut to a calm, uncluttered desk — no chaos, just a single laptop open, content publishing on its own. VO: 'It's that they removed themselves from the production loop entirely. While you're juggling five platforms and a real business, they're not writing, filming, or editing anything.'

BEAT 4 — REVEAL (15–20s): Wide shot — bright, open workspace, a person walking away from their desk confidently while content appears on screens behind them. VO: 'The content just runs. That's the system.'

BEAT 5 — CTA (20–23s): Clean bright end card. VO: 'And you can have it too.'

- **duration_seconds:** 23

**image prompts**

1. A person sitting at a bright, modern desk holding a phone, scrolling through a competitor's social media feed with a look of quiet surprise — clean daylight, soft shadows, minimal clutter, warm natural light through a large window.
2. The same person surrounded by three open devices — phone, tablet, and laptop — all showing different social media platforms simultaneously, a subtle expression of overwhelm on their face, bright open-plan workspace, natural light, no dark tones.
3. A calm, uncluttered modern desk with a single open laptop displaying a blurred colorful dashboard interface with soft abstract UI shapes — no text visible — content tiles faintly appearing on screen, bright and airy atmosphere, no person present, serene and ordered.
4. A confident person walking away from a bright modern workspace, back to camera, while behind them three screens on a clean wall show soft blurred colorful social media grid layouts — abstract, unreadable — daylight flooding the room, open and optimistic mood.

**video concept**

A calm, observational short that follows a cold visitor's silent judgment of a neglected social profile. The visual journey moves from a warm, confident first impression — someone being recommended — to the quiet chill of landing on a profile with no recent activity. The twist: the viewer realizes the damage isn't loud. It's a silent decision made in seconds. The reveal reframes the pain point — it's not about creativity or time, it's about what absence signals. The final beat is reassuring: one URL, first package free.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — OBSERVATION (0–4s): Close-up of a phone screen showing a blurred messaging app — someone tapping a shared profile link. Warm, daylight tone. Voiceover: 'Someone just landed on your LinkedIn. They didn't search for you — a mutual sent them.'

BEAT 2 — MEANING (5–10s): Cut to a person sitting at a bright desk, scrolling slowly upward on a blurred profile feed — the scroll stops, brow slightly furrows. Voiceover: 'Your last post? Eight weeks ago.'

BEAT 3 — TWIST (11–16s): Same person sets the phone face-down on the desk and turns back to their laptop — a quiet, decisive move. Voiceover: 'They don't think you're busy. They think you might not be around anymore.'

BEAT 4 — REVEAL (17–20s): Wide shot of a clean, bright home office — calm and steady. Voiceover: 'That's the damage inconsistency does quietly.'

BEAT 5 — CTA (21–25s): A hand types a short URL into a browser on a laptop with a soft, colorful blurred interface on screen. Voiceover: 'One URL is all it takes to fix it — and your first package is free.'

### Generated Package

- **package_id:** 27c1027d-a981-4fa8-9573-e099286ae44e
- **title:** The Worst-Case Consequence of a Dead Social Profile
- **status:** draft
- **created_at:** 2026-07-01T21:19:02.157864+00:00
- **funnel_stage:** awareness

- **hook:** Someone just Googled your business — and your last post was eight weeks ago.

**voiceover_text**

Someone just Googled your business. They found your Instagram. Last post: eight weeks ago. Here's what they decided: you're either closed, coasting, or not serious. And here's the part that stings — you meant to post. You just never had time. Because running a business already is a full-time job. Content production is a second one nobody signed up for. That's not laziness. That's math. Your website URL is all it takes to fix it.

**subtitles**

Someone just Googled your business. / Last post: eight weeks ago. / Here's what they decided — / you're closed, coasting, or not serious. / And here's the part that stings — / you meant to post. / You just never had time. / Running a business is already a full-time job. / Content production is a second one. / Nobody signed up for that. / That's not laziness. That's math. / Your website URL is all it takes to fix it.

- **scenario:** 

- **CTA type:** sign_up
- **CTA text:** Drop your website URL and get your first content package free — no payment needed.

**video concept**

A fast-paced vertical short that opens on the concrete fear of a cold visitor judging a dormant social profile, pivots to the real reason it happens — content production is a second full-time job, not a character flaw — then lands the reveal: the fix is already sitting in the founder's browser tab. Visual beats escalate from the empty profile moment to the overwhelmed founder to the unexpected simplicity of the solution. Bright, clean, modern aesthetic throughout.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — OBSERVATION (0–4s): Cut to a close-up of a phone screen showing a blurred social profile grid with a clearly dated last post. Voiceover: 'Someone just Googled your business. They found your Instagram. Last post: eight weeks ago.'

BEAT 2 — MEANING (5–11s): Cut to a founder at a busy desk, laptop open, sticky notes everywhere, clearly mid-task on something unrelated to content. Voiceover: 'Here's what they decided: you're either closed, coasting, or not serious. And here's the part that stings — you meant to post. You just never had time.'

BEAT 3 — REVEAL / TWIST (12–18s): Cut to a wide shot of the same founder, now looking calm, single browser tab open. Voiceover: 'Because running a business already is a full-time job. Content production is a second one nobody signed up for. That's not laziness. That's math.'

BEAT 4 — CTA (19–22s): Cut to a clean bright frame, minimal. Voiceover: 'Your website URL is all it takes to fix it.'

- **duration_seconds:** 22

**image prompts**

1. Close-up of a hand holding a smartphone displaying a blurred social media profile grid with clearly sparse, widely spaced post thumbnails suggesting months of inactivity — bright natural light, clean modern aesthetic, soft shadows, no visible text or UI labels on the screen.
2. A founder sitting at a cluttered but energetic desk covered in sticky notes, an open laptop with a soft colorful blurred dashboard on screen, coffee cup nearby — visibly busy and mid-task, daylight streaming through a window, warm and relatable, no text visible anywhere.
3. Wide shot of the same founder leaning back in a chair, arms crossed, staring at the ceiling with a quietly exhausted expression — bright airy home office, clean walls, natural daylight, no text or screens visible.
4. Extreme close-up of a single browser tab on a laptop keyboard, the screen showing abstract soft colorful UI blobs suggesting a simple form or dashboard — clean white desk surface, bright daylight, minimal and calm, no readable text on screen.

- **strategy_angle:** It's not laziness or lack of ideas. It's that content production is a separate full-time job layered on top of running a business. Normalize the struggle — most founders are in this exact position — then hint that the solution isn't more discipline.

## Package 5 of 21

### Strategy Item

- **strategy_item_id:** 6139307e-a1e5-4149-a7d7-bbb93dc44a6a
- **package_index:** 4
- **topic:** Five platforms, one business, and not enough hours in the day
- **angle:** Show the math: TikTok wants vertical video, LinkedIn wants thoughtful text, Instagram wants visuals, Facebook wants community posts, YouTube Shorts wants hooks. Each platform has its own format. For a solo operator, producing for all five is structurally impossible without a dedicated system.
- **funnel_stage:** awareness
- **platform:** tiktok
- **format:** reel
- **priority:** 2

### Generated Package

- **package_id:** bf2381a0-b155-4b4a-afb6-777afa0a7949
- **title:** Five Platforms, One Business, Zero Hours Left
- **status:** draft
- **created_at:** 2026-07-01T21:19:46.244389+00:00
- **funnel_stage:** awareness

- **hook:** I'll be honest — I tracked exactly how long it took me to post one thing across five platforms. I wish I hadn't.

**voiceover_text**

I timed it once. One piece of content, five platforms. TikTok needs vertical video. LinkedIn wants a thoughtful essay. Instagram needs a visual. Facebook wants a community post. YouTube Shorts needs a punchy hook. That's not one task — that's five different jobs. Every single week. No wonder the queue stays empty. One URL into fenrik Studio and all five are done for you.

**subtitles**

I timed it once. / One piece of content. Five platforms. / TikTok: vertical video. / LinkedIn: thoughtful essay. / Instagram: a visual. / Facebook: community post. / YouTube: punchy hook. / That's not one task — that's FIVE different jobs. / Every. Single. Week. / No wonder the queue stays empty. / One URL into fenrik Studio — / and all five are done for you.

- **scenario:** 

- **CTA type:** sign_up
- **CTA text:** Drop your website URL and get your first content package free — no card needed.

**video concept**

A fast-paced vertical short that opens with a candid confession — the creator timed how long cross-platform posting actually takes — then rapidly cuts through each platform's format demands like a checklist that never ends. The twist: what feels like 'one task' is structurally five separate jobs. The payoff lands when the math becomes undeniable and the solution arrives as a single clean action.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — CONFESSION HOOK (0–3s): Close-up of a hand tapping a phone screen, a timer visible on the display. VO: 'I timed it once. One piece of content, five platforms.'

BEAT 2 — UNEXPECTED FACT (3–10s): Rapid-cut montage — a vertical phone frame, a desktop text editor, a styled photo, a casual group chat interface, a widescreen thumbnail. Each cut is a different platform format. VO: 'TikTok needs vertical video. LinkedIn wants a thoughtful essay. Instagram needs a visual. Facebook wants a community post. YouTube Shorts needs a punchy hook.'

BEAT 3 — IMPLICATION / TWIST (10–17s): Wide shot of a person at a desk, surrounded by open browser tabs, looking at the clock. VO: 'That's not one task — that's five different jobs. Every single week. No wonder the queue stays empty.'

BEAT 4 — PAYOFF + CTA (17–23s): Clean, bright frame — a single hand types a URL into a simple form field, then leans back, relaxed. VO: 'One URL into fenrik Studio and all five are done for you.'

- **duration_seconds:** 23

**image prompts**

1. Bright, clean close-up of a human hand holding a modern smartphone, a soft glowing timer interface visible on the screen — blurred, unreadable, abstract — natural daylight, white desk surface, warm and open feel. No text or labels anywhere in the frame.
2. Fast-paced flat-lay composition: five distinct device frames arranged side by side on a bright white surface — a tall vertical phone, a wide laptop with a blurred colorful screen, a tablet showing soft abstract UI shapes, a second phone in landscape, and a small square frame — each screen showing a different blurred color palette, no readable content. Clean daylight, modern minimal style.
3. Wide-angle shot of a person sitting at a bright modern desk, multiple browser windows open on a monitor showing abstract colorful blobs (not readable), the person's posture slightly slumped, glancing toward a wall clock. Soft natural light, airy room, no text visible anywhere.
4. Clean, minimal overhead shot of a single hand typing on a laptop keyboard, the screen showing a simple blurred form field with a soft gradient — nothing readable. Bright daylight, white desk, a relaxed coffee cup nearby. Open and trustworthy feel.

- **hook:** Why does 'post on social this week' keep surviving every sprint — but never actually getting done?

**video concept**

Tone is blunt and impatient with the problem, never with the viewer. Pacing is clipped — one idea per beat, no lingering.

**video script**

BEAT 2 — MISTAKE (3–8s): Cut to a close-up of a cluttered sprint board with one sticky note that's clearly been there too long. Voiceover: 'Here's the mistake — you're treating social content like something you'll eventually get to.'

BEAT 4 — CORRECT APPROACH + CTA (16–23s): Cut to a clean desk, someone typing a URL into a browser — calm, simple, solved. Voiceover: 'The fix isn't hiring someone. It's stopping the bleed. Your website URL is all it takes to get your first content package — completely free.'

### Generated Package

- **package_id:** 897b0282-39ea-4bdb-b448-bdb68f532219
- **title:** The Mistake That Costs You Customers Before They Ever Reach Out
- **status:** draft
- **created_at:** 2026-07-01T21:22:12.504314+00:00
- **funnel_stage:** problem_aware

- **hook:** Your product is live, your site looks great — and a prospect just decided you're probably not worth contacting.

**voiceover_text**

Your product is live, your site looks great — and a prospect just decided you're probably not worth contacting. Here's what happened: they searched for you, found your social profile, and your last post was three months ago. That's not a minor detail. To them, it reads as: nobody's home. The mistake isn't ignoring social. It's assuming a dormant profile is neutral. It isn't. Fix the gap — before the next prospect makes the same call.

**subtitles**

Your product is live. Your site looks great. / A prospect just decided you're not worth contacting. / They searched for you. / Found your profile. / Last post: three months ago. / That's not neutral. / It reads as: nobody's home. / The mistake isn't ignoring social. / It's assuming a dormant profile doesn't cost you anything. / It does. / Fix the gap — before the next prospect makes the same call.

- **scenario:** 

- **CTA type:** sign_up
- **CTA text:** Share your website URL and get your first content package free — no payment required.

**video concept**

A fast-paced vertical short built on contrast: a polished, active business website versus a completely dormant social profile. The video opens on the contrast (live product vs. silent social), names the mistake (assuming inactivity is neutral), shows why it backfires (the silent judgment a prospect makes), pivots to the correct approach (keeping the profile active is a trust signal, not a vanity metric), and closes on the CTA. Visual beats escalate from the clean, confident business moment to the cold, empty-feeling profile moment, then resolve into an active, content-filled feed. Reporter tone throughout — factual, no drama, just the observation.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — MISTAKE (0–5s): Open on a confident founder at a clean desk, clearly mid-workday, focused. A brief cut to a phone showing a blurred social profile with a long gap between posts — visually sparse, clearly inactive. VOICEOVER: 'Your product is live, your site looks great — and a prospect just decided you're probably not worth contacting.' BEAT 2 — WHY IT BACKFIRES (5–13s): Cut to a person casually scrolling on their phone, pausing on a profile, then swiping away. The social profile on screen looks sparse, dated. VOICEOVER: 'Here's what happened: they searched for you, found your social profile, and your last post was three months ago. That's not a minor detail. To them, it reads as: nobody's home.' BEAT 3 — CORRECT APPROACH (13–20s): Cut to the same phone now showing a lively, consistently updated social feed — colorful, active, recent posts visible. The founder glances at it briefly, then goes back to actual work. VOICEOVER: 'The mistake isn't ignoring social. It's assuming a dormant profile is neutral. It isn't. Fix the gap — before the next prospect makes the same call.' BEAT 4 — CTA (20–23s): Clean end card with soft background. VOICEOVER: 'Share your website URL and get your first content package free — no payment required.'

- **duration_seconds:** 23

## Package 9 of 21

### Strategy Item

- **strategy_item_id:** 559329a3-d35b-4ca2-9e66-6f49105f8abe
- **package_index:** 8
- **topic:** Hiring a freelance content creator: what it actually costs and what you actually get
- **angle:** Break down the real cost of hiring — rates, briefing time, revision rounds, platform adaptation, management overhead. For most small businesses, the math doesn't work. This isn't an attack on freelancers; it's an honest look at why the model breaks down at small scale.
- **funnel_stage:** problem_aware
- **platform:** tiktok
- **format:** reel
- **priority:** 1
- **trend_id:** 
- **topic_id:** 
- **strategy_id:** 23efd70f-823b-475c-9839-7e959e0bd55e
- **parent strategy name:** fenrik Studio: From Empty Queue to Ready-to-Post — Social Content Without the Work

**brief JSON**

- **package_id:** dfaf42a2-5512-400a-b2be-ca60d495ffbc
- **title:** The Overlooked Line Item in Every Freelancer Hire
- **status:** draft
- **created_at:** 2026-07-01T21:22:56.546534+00:00
- **funnel_stage:** problem_aware

- **hook:** Hiring a freelance content creator looks cheap — until you count the hours you spend managing one.

**voiceover_text**

You hire a freelancer. Day rate looks fine. Then comes the brief. The back-and-forth. The revision round. The version that's great for Instagram but completely wrong for LinkedIn. You're four hours in and nothing is posted yet. That's the part nobody puts in the invoice. The real cost of freelance content isn't the rate — it's the management overhead nobody warned you about.

**subtitles**

Hiring a freelancer looks cheap.
Until you count the hours you spend managing one.

Day rate? Fine.
Then comes the brief.
The back-and-forth.
The revision round.
The version that works for Instagram — but not LinkedIn.

You're four hours in.
Nothing is posted yet.

That's the part nobody puts in the invoice.

The real cost isn't the rate.
It's the overhead nobody warned you about.

- **scenario:** 

- **CTA type:** sign_up
- **CTA text:** Paste your website URL and get your first content package free — no payment needed.

**video concept**

A fast-paced vertical short that opens mid-scene: a business owner sitting at a laptop looking satisfied after hiring a freelancer. The mood quickly shifts as a cascade of messages, revision requests, and platform-specific rewrites pile up. The twist lands hard — the 'affordable' hire quietly consumed an entire workday. The resolution reframes the real problem: it was never the rate, it was the management overhead. Clean, bright, modern visuals throughout. No dark or thriller tone.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — SETUP (0–4s): Business owner at a bright, modern desk. Relaxed. Just hit send on a freelancer hire. Voiceover: 'You hire a freelancer. Day rate looks fine.'

BEAT 2 — CONFLICT (4–12s): Cut to rapid-fire visual beats — a brief document being typed, a chat thread filling with back-and-forth messages, a revision note, a second revision note. Voiceover: 'Then comes the brief. The back-and-forth. The revision round. The version that's great for Instagram but completely wrong for LinkedIn.'

BEAT 3 — TWIST (12–18s): Wide shot of the same business owner, now visibly drained, staring at the screen. Clock on the wall (or implied time-lapse). Nothing published. Voiceover: 'You're four hours in and nothing is posted yet. That's the part nobody puts in the invoice.'

BEAT 4 — RESOLUTION + CTA (18–23s): Clean cut to a calm, bright frame. Business owner closes the laptop. Voiceover: 'The real cost of freelance content isn't the rate — it's the management overhead nobody warned you about.' Text CTA appears on screen: 'Paste your website URL. First package free.'

- **duration_seconds:** 23

**image prompts**

1. A bright, modern home office. A person in casual business attire sits at a clean wooden desk, smiling at a laptop with a blurred generic dashboard on screen. Natural daylight from a large window. Relaxed, satisfied energy. Clean and minimal.
2. Close-up of a laptop screen showing a blurred, abstract chat interface with multiple message bubbles stacking up rapidly — colorful, unreadable, busy. The screen glows softly. Hands visible on the keyboard, slightly tense. Bright room, soft shadows.
3. The same person from the first image, now leaning back in the chair with arms crossed, visibly tired. The desk is slightly more cluttered — a coffee cup, a notepad with abstract scribbles. The laptop screen shows blurred colorful UI blobs. Daylight still present but slightly dimmer, suggesting time has passed.
4. Wide shot of the desk from above. The laptop is closed. A notepad with abstract marks lies beside it. Nothing appears to have been published — no sense of completion. Clean, airy, slightly empty feeling. Bright natural light.

- **strategy_angle:** Break down the real cost of hiring — rates, briefing time, revision rounds, platform adaptation, management overhead. For most small businesses, the math doesn't work. This isn't an attack on freelancers; it's an honest look at why the model breaks down at small scale.

### Generated Package

- **package_id:** b1bb91a0-7d2d-489d-9939-30b934e4566e
- **title:** The Content Idea Graveyard: Why Great Ideas Never Become Posts
- **status:** draft
- **created_at:** 2026-07-01T21:25:31.372731+00:00
- **funnel_stage:** problem_aware

- **hook:** Why does every great content idea you have end up buried in a notes app you never open again?

**voiceover_text**

You had the idea. Customer win. Product update. A story worth telling. You typed it into your notes app at 11pm and thought — I'll post this tomorrow. That was four months ago. The idea is still there. So are nineteen others. The problem was never the ideas. It was the gap between idea and published post — and that gap is costing you your presence on every platform at once.

**subtitles**

You had the idea.
Customer win. Product update. A story worth telling.
Typed it into your notes at 11pm.
I'll post this tomorrow.
That was four months ago.
The idea is still there.
So are nineteen others.
The problem was never the ideas.
It was the gap between idea and published post.
And that gap is costing you your presence on every platform at once.

- **scenario:** 

- **CTA type:** sign_up
- **CTA text:** Give us your website URL — your first content package is on us, no payment needed.

**video concept**

A fast vertical short that opens on a founder's notes app crammed with unposted ideas at midnight — the setup. We pull back to reveal every social platform sitting silent and empty — the conflict. The twist: the ideas were never the problem; the production gap was. Resolution: one URL is all it takes to close that gap. The mood is sharp, slightly fed-up, and relatable — not a lecture, one tight scene.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — SETUP (0–4s)
Close-up on a phone screen: a notes app overflowing with half-formed ideas — customer wins, feature updates, product angles. Timestamp on the newest note: 11:47 PM.
VO: 'You had the idea. Customer win. Product update. A story worth telling. You typed it into your notes app at 11pm and thought — I'll post this tomorrow.'

BEAT 2 — CONFLICT (5–12s)
Cut to: a grid of social platform icons — all showing zero recent activity. Profiles collecting dust. Follower counts frozen.
VO: 'That was four months ago. The idea is still there. So are nineteen others.'

BEAT 3 — TWIST (13–18s)
Cut to: the founder staring at the notes app, then at a blank scheduler — the realization hits.
VO: 'The problem was never the ideas. It was the gap between idea and published post.'

BEAT 4 — RESOLUTION + CTA (19–24s)
Cut to: a clean, bright workspace. One browser tab open. A single URL typed in. Content appearing across multiple platforms simultaneously.
VO: 'And that gap is costing you your presence on every platform at once. Give us your website URL — your first content package is on us, no payment needed.'
Text overlay: fenrik.studio

- **duration_seconds:** 24

**image prompts**

1. Extreme close-up of a smartphone screen showing a notes app filled with dozens of short text entries, the list scrolling far beyond the visible frame, shot in warm late-night ambient light from a desk lamp — the screen glows softly in an otherwise dim but not dark room, clean modern desk surface visible at the edges, photorealistic, bright screen contrast against a softly lit background
2. Wide shot of a clean modern home office desk from above, a laptop open showing a blurred abstract social media dashboard with muted colorful UI blobs and no readable text, surrounded by a coffee mug and scattered sticky notes — bright natural daylight from a window, soft shadows, airy and open feel, photorealistic
3. Medium shot of a young professional sitting at a desk, leaning back in their chair, arms crossed, staring at their phone with a flat expression of quiet frustration — bright modern workspace, large window with daylight, clean minimal decor, no text or screens readable, photorealistic, candid and relatable
4. Overhead flat-lay of a clean white desk with a single laptop open, the screen showing soft blurred abstract colorful interface shapes suggesting multiple social platform windows open simultaneously — bright natural light, minimal props, airy and modern, no readable text anywhere, photorealistic
5. Close-up of two hands typing a single short line of text into a clean browser address bar on a laptop keyboard — bright daylight workspace, shallow depth of field blurring the background into soft warm tones, modern and purposeful feeling, no readable text visible, photorealistic

### Generated Package

- **package_id:** 1de1a1f6-3bcf-44ad-8f3a-e2ffd63ccf6c
- **title:** The Agency Owner Who Can't Maintain Their Own Social Presence
- **status:** draft
- **created_at:** 2026-07-01T21:27:14.221459+00:00
- **funnel_stage:** problem_aware

- **hook:** I'll be honest — our agency's own Instagram hadn't been touched in two months while we were busy posting for clients every single day.

**voiceover_text**

Here's the part no one talks about: the people who know exactly how to do social media are often the ones with the emptiest accounts. Not because they don't care — because client work eats everything first. And when a potential client checks your profile and sees nothing? They don't ask why. They just leave. Bandwidth isn't a skills problem. It's a capacity problem. Your website URL is all it takes to get your first content package — completely free.

**subtitles**

The people who know social best... often have the emptiest accounts. | Not a skills problem. A bandwidth problem. | A cold visitor doesn't ask why. They just leave. | Your website URL is all it takes. First package — free.

- **scenario:** An agency owner pitches a new client on social media management, then realizes they cannot keep up with content production for their own agency's accounts while handling client work.

- **CTA type:** sign_up
- **CTA text:** Give us your website URL — your first content package is on us, no payment required.

**video concept**

Open on a professional, bright agency workspace — someone clearly mid-flow on client work. Fast cut to their own brand's social profile: visually sparse, last post buried far back. The twist lands here: this person knows everything about content — and still fell behind. The final beat reframes it: it was never about skill, it was about capacity. End on a calm, reassuring close with the free package offer.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — UNEXPECTED FACT (0–5s): Close-up of hands typing fast at a clean agency desk, multiple browser tabs visible with blurred client dashboards. Voiceover: 'I'll be honest — our agency's own Instagram hadn't been touched in two months while we were busy posting for clients every single day.'

BEAT 2 — IMPLICATION (5–14s): Cut to a bright phone screen showing a sparse, inactive social profile — last post visually far down the scroll. Voiceover: 'The people who know exactly how to do social media are often the ones with the emptiest accounts. Not because they don't care — because client work eats everything first. And when a potential client checks your profile and sees nothing? They don't ask why. They just leave.'

BEAT 3 — PROOF / REFRAME (14–20s): Cut to a calm, tidy desk scene — a single laptop open with a blurred colorful interface, one coffee cup, relaxed energy. Voiceover: 'Bandwidth isn't a skills problem. It's a capacity problem.'

BEAT 4 — CTA (20–25s): Bright, clean end frame — no clutter, calm and trustworthy. Voiceover: 'Your website URL is all it takes to get your first content package — completely free.'

- **duration_seconds:** 25

**image prompts**

1. Bright, modern open-plan agency office in natural daylight. A professional in their 30s sits at a clean white desk, leaning forward, fully focused on a large monitor showing blurred colorful browser tabs. Multiple notebooks and a coffee cup nearby. Energy is busy and purposeful. Soft shadows, airy and well-lit. Photorealistic.

4. Minimalist bright workspace: a single open laptop on a white desk with a blurred abstract colorful interface on screen — soft UI blobs, no readable content. One ceramic coffee cup. Clean, uncluttered, trustworthy. Warm natural light. The overall feel is calm and reassuring. Photorealistic.

- **strategy_angle:** An agency that sells social media services to clients has its own accounts sitting empty. The irony is real and common — when you're deep in client delivery, your own brand is the first thing to go. Use this to show that the problem isn't skill or knowledge, it's bandwidth.

### Generated Package

- **package_id:** 5a84cd08-d67d-4987-8c5d-40d34640b4f7
- **title:** The Routine That's Quietly Draining Your Week — And Your Instagram
- **status:** draft
- **created_at:** 2026-07-01T21:28:02.191839+00:00
- **funnel_stage:** problem_aware

- **hook:** How many hours did you spend on social content this week — and how much of it actually went live?

**voiceover_text**

Here's the mistake: ecommerce brands treat content like a weekly task. Carve out time, film something, edit, caption, post. Repeat forever. But that routine is quietly eating your week — and when a warm prospect clicks your Instagram after seeing your ad, they land on a ghost account. No posts. No proof. No reason to trust you. The fix isn't more hours. It's removing content from your weekly routine entirely.

**subtitles**

How many hours did you spend on social content this week — and how much of it actually went live? // Here's the mistake: treating content like a weekly task. // Carve out time. Film. Edit. Caption. Post. Repeat. // That routine is eating your week — // and when a warm prospect clicks your Instagram after seeing your ad — // they land on a ghost account. // No posts. No proof. No reason to trust you. // The fix isn't more hours. // It's removing content from your weekly routine entirely.

- **scenario:** A small ecommerce brand owner schedules time on Friday afternoon to film a TikTok, but the shoot runs long and the footage sits unedited through the entire weekend.

- **CTA type:** sign_up
- **CTA text:** Give us your website URL and get your first content package free — no payment, no routine required.

**video concept**

A fast-paced vertical short that dramatizes the painful irony of an ecommerce brand spending hours every week on content — only for their Instagram to still look dead when a warm ad prospect checks it. Opens on a pointed question about wasted hours, pivots to the mistake of treating content as a recurring manual task, shows the consequence (a warm lead landing on a dormant profile), then reveals the correct approach — removing content production from the weekly grind entirely. Ends on a clean CTA.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — HOOK (0–4s): Text on screen: 'How many hours on content this week?' Voiceover asks the hook question over a shot of someone at a desk, looking at their phone with a tired expression. Fast cut.

BEAT 2 — MISTAKE (4–9s): Quick montage feel — person filming on phone, switching apps, typing a caption, closing the laptop without posting. Voiceover names the mistake: the weekly content routine.

BEAT 3 — WHY IT BACKFIRES (9–16s): Cut to a phone screen showing a blurred, sparse Instagram profile — no recent posts visible. Voiceover delivers the gut punch: a warm prospect from your ad just landed here. Ghost account. No social proof.

BEAT 4 — CORRECT APPROACH (16–21s): Bright, clean cut. Person at desk, relaxed, no filming setup. Voiceover: the fix is removing content from the routine entirely.

BEAT 5 — CTA (21–25s): Clean end card. Voiceover CTA. URL prompt on screen.

- **duration_seconds:** 25

**image prompts**

1. Bright, clean overhead shot of a person sitting at a modern home-office desk, staring at their phone with a tired, slightly frustrated expression, coffee going cold beside them, soft natural daylight from a window, no text or screens visible
2. Close-up of a hand holding a smartphone angled toward a small product flatlay on a table, mid-setup for filming, items slightly scattered and unfinished, warm natural light, clean background — conveying the effort of manual content production without any readable text on the screen
3. A phone held in one hand displaying a blurred, sparse social media profile grid — only one or two faint image blobs visible in the grid, the rest empty, soft shallow depth of field, bright neutral background, no readable text or UI labels anywhere on screen
4. A calm, uncluttered modern desk scene — laptop open showing abstract soft-colored dashboard blobs on screen, person leaning back relaxed with arms crossed, bright daylight, no filming gear in sight — conveying ease and the absence of manual effort

You write a LinkedIn post. Then you realize Instagram needs a different format. TikTok needs a reshoot. Facebook needs a rewrite. One URL is all it takes to end that cycle. Your first package is free.

**video concept**

A fast-paced vertical short that opens on a founder confidently typing a LinkedIn post — the 'before' moment. Then the twist: a rapid-fire visual sequence shows the same idea fragmenting into four distinct platform tasks, each one demanding something different. The energy shifts from calm to overwhelmed. The payoff is a clean contrast — one URL input replacing all that chaos — landing just before the CTA.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — HOOK (0–3s): Founder at a clean desk, typing with focus. VO: 'You think you're making one piece of content.' BEAT 2 — UNEXPECTED FACT / TWIST (3–10s): Fast cuts — LinkedIn draft, then Instagram layout, then a phone propped up for a TikTok reshoot, then a Facebook rewrite on screen. VO: 'You're actually making four. LinkedIn, Instagram, TikTok, Facebook — same idea, four separate production tasks.' BEAT 3 — IMPLICATION (10–17s): Founder slumps back, tabs open everywhere, energy drained. VO: 'Most teams quietly give up somewhere in the middle. That's not a creativity problem. That's a platform fragmentation problem.' BEAT 4 — PAYOFF / PROOF (17–22s): Clean desk again — just a browser tab open with a website URL. VO: 'One URL is all it takes to end that cycle. **image prompts**

The mood is confident and settled, like the start of a productive task. Soft morning light through a large window. No text, no screens with readable content, no visible words anywhere in the frame.
2. The same clean desk, now showing four separate devices arranged side by side — a laptop, a tablet, a smartphone propped upright, and a second open notebook. Each screen shows a blurred, abstract interface with soft colorful UI blobs — unreadable, distinct in layout from each other. The person's hands are visible, hovering between devices, mid-motion. The composition feels slightly overwhelming — too many things at once. Bright daylight still, but the frame feels busier and more fragmented.
3. Close-up of a person's face, slightly leaning back in their chair, expression quietly drained — not dramatic, just tired. Eyes unfocused, looking slightly off-frame. A blurred background of soft monitor glow and open tabs. Clean, modern space. Natural light. The mood is 'I thought this would take twenty minutes.' 4. A clean, minimal desk scene — just one laptop open, one browser tab visible as a soft abstract blur. The person's hand rests calmly on the trackpad. The room is bright and uncluttered. The twist: it's not their ideas that are missing, it's the production infrastructure. The video escalates through the hidden cost of that gap (agency pricing, lost hours), then lands on a clean, reassuring payoff: the production problem is already solved.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — UNEXPECTED FACT (0–5s): Open on a confident professional at a bright modern desk, staring at a blank screen. Voiceover: 'You're calling it a creativity block. It isn't.' 1. Bright, clean home office scene in natural daylight. A confident professional in their 30s sits at a modern wooden desk, hands resting on a keyboard, looking calmly at a laptop screen showing a soft blurred colorful interface. Expression is composed but still — the kind of stillness before a decision. Warm ambient light, minimal clutter, open and airy feel.
2. Close-up of a laptop screen displaying a blurred, abstract document with vague columns of figures — unreadable but clearly a pricing or quote layout. The background is softly out of focus, a bright modern workspace. No visible text or numbers. The mood is calm but the visual implies a cost.
3. Wide shot of a tidy, sunlit desk. A phone lies face-up showing soft abstract colorful icons representing multiple social platforms — blurred and stylized, not branded. A coffee cup sits nearby. The scene feels organized and modern, a contrast to the earlier frozen moment. Bright, open, optimistic.
4. Minimal clean end-card style scene: a soft white-to-light-grey gradient background with a single small plant and a phone displaying a blurred pastel dashboard interface. Calm, trustworthy, professional. No text visible anywhere in the image. Natural light, open composition.

### Quick alignment fields

- **strategy_topic:** Running out of things to say: the content block that isn't about creativity
- **strategy_angle:** A solo consultant has plenty of expertise but hits a wall every time they open a blank post. The block isn't a lack of knowledge — it's the pressure to produce something platform-appropriate, engaging, and on-brand from scratch, alone, every week. Reframe content block as a production problem, not a creativity problem.
- **generated_title:** The Content Block That's Costing You More Than You Think
- **generated_hook:** You're calling it a creativity block — but you're actually paying for a production problem.
- **generated_scenario:** 
- **generated_cta:** Hand us your website URL — your first content package is free, no payment required.

## Package 16 of 21

### Strategy Item

- **strategy_item_id:** 3134103e-4fe2-4583-b7c6-752d64a63fb8
- **package_index:** 15
- **topic:** When content production starts eating into the hours you need to run the business
- **angle:** A small marketing team at an AI startup spends more time trying to produce content than shipping product updates or talking to customers. Content was supposed to support the business — instead it became a second job. Show how the production burden quietly displaces higher-value work.
- **funnel_stage:** problem_aware
- **platform:** tiktok
- **format:** reel
- **priority:** 1

- **topic_id:**

### Generated Package

- **package_id:** 81214c93-15a9-454d-90dd-575b565003ef
- **title:** You Hired Yourself as the Content Team — That Was the Mistake
- **status:** draft
- **created_at:** 2026-07-01T21:30:22.853036+00:00
- **funnel_stage:** problem_aware

- **hook:** You're running a business — and somehow you also became the scriptwriter, the video editor, and the social media manager.

**voiceover_text**

Here's the thing nobody tells you when you start a company: content production is a full-time job hiding inside your actual job. You sit down to write one post. An hour later you're color-correcting a clip you never meant to film. The product update? Still waiting. The customer call? Rescheduled. Turns out you didn't hire a content team — you just quietly became one. Your website URL is all we need. First package is free.

**subtitles**

You're running a business — and somehow you're also the scriptwriter, editor, and social manager. // Content production is a full-time job hiding inside your actual job. // You sit down to write one post. // An hour later you're color-correcting a clip you never meant to film. // The product update? Still waiting. // The customer call? Rescheduled. // You didn't hire a content team — you just quietly became one. // Your website URL is all we need. First package is free.

- **scenario:** 

- **CTA type:** sign_up
- **CTA text:** Give us your website URL — your first content package is on us. No payment, no content team required.

**video concept**

A fast, self-aware vertical short told from an insider POV — the kind of thing only someone who has lived inside a small team would say out loud. The tone is light and comedic but the truth lands hard. Opens on a relatable 'productive-looking' scene that quickly reveals the absurdity: a founder deep in video editing software when they should be doing literally anything else. The unexpected turn is the punchline — they didn't fail to hire a content team, they accidentally became one. The fix is delivered straight and seriously at the end.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — SITUATION (0–5s): Wide shot of a person at a desk looking intensely focused — multiple browser tabs open, headphones on, clearly 'in the zone.' Text burn-in: 'Crushing it today.' 

BEAT 2 — UNEXPECTED TURN (5–13s): Cut to a close-up reveal — they're not in their product dashboard or on a customer call. They're deep inside a video editing timeline, nudging a clip by two frames. Cut to their phone: a customer message sits unanswered. Cut back to the screen: a half-finished caption doc. Text burn-in: 'Wait — is this… your job?' 

BEAT 3 — PUNCHLINE (13–19s): Quick cut to the person leaning back, staring at the ceiling with the slow realization of someone who just understood a joke about themselves. Text burn-in: 'You didn't forget to hire a content team. You just became one.' 

BEAT 4 — CTA (19–24s): Clean cut to a calm, bright frame. Voiceover delivers the fix straight. Text burn-in: 'Give us your URL. First content package is free.'

- **duration_seconds:** 24

**image prompts**

1. Bright, modern home office scene: a person sitting at a clean desk, headphones on, leaning forward with intense focus toward a laptop with a blurred, colorful abstract interface on screen — the body language reads 'deep in work,' natural daylight from a side window, warm and energetic atmosphere, vertical 9:16 composition.
2. Close-up of a person's hands on a keyboard, with a smartphone placed beside the laptop showing a blurred messaging app with an unanswered notification glow — the laptop screen shows abstract colorful editing-style UI blobs, soft daylight, slightly cluttered desk suggesting a busy session, vertical 9:16 composition.
3. Medium shot of the same person leaning back in their chair, arms loosely at their sides, staring at the ceiling with a slow, dawning expression — half-amused, half-exhausted — the desk behind them still glowing with the abstract screen, bright airy room, vertical 9:16 composition.
4. Clean, minimal bright frame: a person's hand relaxed on a desk next to a laptop showing a soft abstract blurred interface — calm, uncluttered, open space, daylight flooding in, the mood shifts from chaos to relief, vertical 9:16 composition.

**video concept**

A calm, observational short that walks through the overlooked detail of a done-for-you content delivery. Opens with a confession-style hook about not knowing what 'ready to post' really means. Cuts through a visual journey: a URL typed into a browser, then the inbox moment — a delivery arrives. The reveal is the specific contents: a short-form video, platform-formatted captions, hashtags. The twist is reframing the output not as 'content' but as a 'publishing kit' — something most people don't realize they're missing. Ends on a calm, direct CTA. Pacing is unhurried but tight. No frantic cuts. Steady and trustworthy.

### Generated Package

- **package_id:** 111f94e1-f191-4d90-98ab-665e095552f2
- **title:** Two People, Five Platforms — The Math Nobody Talks About
- **status:** draft
- **created_at:** 2026-07-01T21:31:55.250068+00:00
- **funnel_stage:** solution_aware

- **hook:** A two-person team can stay active on five platforms. You just can't be the ones producing the content.

**voiceover_text**

Here's the myth: a small team can manage five social platforms if they just get organized. Wrong. Organization doesn't create videos. It just schedules the panic. The real fix isn't a better system — it's removing production from your plate entirely. One URL in. A full batch of ready-to-post videos and platform assets out. Your team's only job? Hit schedule. That's the math that actually works.

**subtitles**

MYTH: Get organized and you can handle five platforms.
REALITY: Organization doesn't make videos.
One URL in → full batch of ready-to-post content out.
Your only job: hit schedule.

- **scenario:** 

- **CTA type:** sign_up
- **CTA text:** Give us your URL — your first content package is free, no payment required.

**video concept**

Fast contrarian vertical short. Opens on a split-second high-pressure moment — a two-person team at a laptop late afternoon, deadline energy, five platform tabs open, nothing queued. Voiceover immediately breaks the myth. Visual beats shift from chaos to clarity: the moment they submit a URL, a batch of content arrives ready to post. The final beat is calm — one person clicks schedule, done. Tone is conspiratorial and direct, like an insider letting you in on what actually works.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — COMMON BELIEF [0–4s]: Two people, five platforms, zero content queued. Cut to a frantic desk scene — multiple browser tabs, blank drafts, a clock on the wall. VO: 'Here's the myth: a small team can manage five social platforms if they just get organized.'

BEAT 2 — WHY WRONG [5–12s]: Quick cut to a to-do list that keeps growing. VO: 'Wrong. Organization doesn't create videos. It just schedules the panic. The real fix isn't a better system — it's removing production from your plate entirely.'

BEAT 3 — PROOF / TWIST [13–19s]: One person types a website URL into a clean interface. Cut to a bright, tidy screen showing a batch of content assets — videos, captions, platform posts — all ready. VO: 'One URL in. A full batch of ready-to-post videos and platform assets out.'

BEAT 4 — PAYOFF + CTA [20–24s]: Same person, now relaxed, clicks a single button. VO: 'Your team's only job? Hit schedule. That's the math that actually works.'

- **duration_seconds:** 24

- **strategy_angle:** Show the practical math: a small team submits their website URL once and receives a batch of ready-to-post videos and platform assets. No internal production time, no freelancer management. The team's only job is to schedule and post. Connect this directly to the bandwidth problem small teams face.

### Strategy Item

- **strategy_item_id:** c9252405-2453-4f3a-9d64-b23e8806d75c
- **package_index:** 18
- **topic:** Why a fixed monthly package beats an unpredictable agency retainer for small businesses
- **angle:** Compare the experience: an agency retainer involves contracts, kickoff calls, briefs, revisions, and invoices that vary. A fixed package means a known output at a known price. For founders and small teams who need predictability, the difference matters. Reference the 5, 10, and 20 video package tiers without overselling.
- **funnel_stage:** solution_aware
- **platform:** tiktok
- **format:** reel
- **priority:** 2

### Generated Package

- **package_id:** c3293d78-d6e7-4da7-b5a8-dbbb8e8b903f
- **title:** The Retainer That Kept Changing Its Mind
- **status:** draft
- **created_at:** 2026-07-01T21:32:43.752489+00:00
- **funnel_stage:** solution_aware

- **hook:** Your first content package is free — and most people only care about that after they've already paid an agency three months of invoices they didn't expect.

**voiceover_text**

You hired an agency. Signed a contract. Sat through a kickoff call. Wrote a brief. Waited for revisions. Got an invoice that was somehow different from last month's. And your social content? Still not live. Here's the twist: a fixed package — 5, 10, or 20 videos — tells you the price before you say yes. No surprises. No calls. Just content. And the first package? Free.

**subtitles**

You hired an agency. / Signed a contract. / Sat through a kickoff call. / Wrote a brief. / Waited for revisions. / Got an invoice that was somehow... different. / And your social content? / Still not live. / Here's the twist: / 5, 10, or 20 videos. / Fixed price. / No surprises. No calls. / Just content. / First package? Free.

- **scenario:** 

- **CTA type:** sign_up
- **CTA text:** Give us your website URL — your first content package is completely free, no invoice surprises.

**video concept**

A fast-paced vertical short that dramatizes the chaos of an agency retainer — contracts, kickoff calls, revision loops, mystery invoices — then pivots hard to the calm simplicity of a fixed package. The visual tone shifts from cluttered and tense to clean and resolved. The punchline lands on the free first package as the unexpected, almost absurd contrast to everything the viewer just watched.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — SITUATION (0–5s): Quick-cut montage of a founder's desk: a thick contract being slid across, a calendar invite for 'Kickoff Call' appearing on a blurred screen, a stack of sticky note briefs. Energy is slightly frantic. Voiceover: 'You hired an agency. Signed a contract. Sat through a kickoff call. Wrote a brief.'

BEAT 2 — UNEXPECTED TURN (5–13s): A revision email notification pops up (shown as a blurred UI blob on a phone screen), then a paper invoice lands on the desk — clearly a different number than expected. The founder stares at it, head tilting. Voiceover: 'Waited for revisions. Got an invoice that was somehow different from last month's. And your social content? Still not live.'

BEAT 3 — PUNCHLINE (13–20s): Hard cut to a clean, bright desk. A single laptop with a soft abstract dashboard glow. Calm. One number on screen (blurred, unreadable). Voiceover: 'Here's the twist: a fixed package — 5, 10, or 20 videos — tells you the price before you say yes. No surprises. No calls. Just content.'

BEAT 4 — CTA (20–24s): Founder smiles at the screen, relaxed. Voiceover: 'And the first package? Free.' Burned-in subtitle: 'Give us your website URL — first package is free.'

- **duration_seconds:** 24

**image prompts**

1. Bright, clean modern office desk in natural daylight — a thick stack of printed papers and a pen being placed on top, a laptop open in the background showing a blurred colorful calendar interface, slightly cluttered but not dark; warm, professional atmosphere, vertical crop
2. Close-up of a person's hand holding a printed paper invoice, expression off-frame, the paper slightly crumpled at the corner as if picked up in surprise; clean white desk surface, soft daylight from the side, vertical crop, no visible text or numbers on the paper
3. A founder sitting at a bright modern desk, leaning back in their chair with a slightly bewildered, dry-humor expression — not distressed, more 'I can't believe this is the process'; clean background, natural light, relaxed but skeptical energy, vertical crop
4. Hard visual contrast: same desk, now clear and uncluttered — a single open laptop with a soft abstract blurred dashboard glow on screen, one coffee cup, calm and minimal; bright daylight, clean modern aesthetic, vertical crop, no readable text on screen
5. A person smiling at a laptop screen, relaxed posture, hand resting on the desk — the screen shows a soft blurred colorful interface, nothing readable; bright clean background, open airy space, natural daylight, calm and resolved energy, vertical crop

**video concept**

A fast vertical short built on the contrarian MODE BEATS: open on the common belief (inactive accounts are just embarrassing), flip it hard (they are actively losing you customers), show the proof (a prospect silently chooses a competitor who looks active), then land the payoff (the fix is already sitting on your website — one URL in, full batch out). Visual escalation: quiet profile screen → competitor's busy feed → the moment a prospect makes a silent decision → the simple input-output reveal. Annoyed Operator voice — clipped, a little fed up, no filler. Hook loop opens on 'embarrassing vs. costing you' and closes late on 'the content was already there.'

**video script**

BEAT 1 — COMMON BELIEF (0–4s)
Visual: A person glancing at their own sparse social profile on a phone, relaxed, unbothered.
VO: 'Everyone thinks a quiet social account just looks a bit unprofessional.'

BEAT 2 — WHY WRONG / TWIST (4–12s)
Visual: Cut to a prospect on a laptop, comparing two profiles side by side — one active, one silent. The prospect's hand moves toward the active one.
VO: 'Wrong. It's actively costing you. A prospect finds your product, checks your profile, sees nothing posted in months — and walks straight to whoever looks alive.'

BEAT 3 — PROOF / PAYOFF (12–20s)
Visual: Clean, bright shot — a website URL typed into a simple interface, then a rapid fan of formatted social posts and a video thumbnail appearing on screen.
VO: 'The content was already on your website. One URL. A full batch of platform-ready posts and videos, out the other side. No brief. No editing. No excuses.'

BEAT 4 — CTA (20–24s)
Visual: End card — clean background, fenrik Studio branding, simple text prompt.
VO: (none — on-screen text carries it)
On-screen: 'Submit your website URL. First package is free.'

- **duration_seconds:** 24

**image prompts**

2. 3. Dramatic tight shot of an empty office chair at a tidy desk, laptop open with a soft abstract blurred dashboard on screen, no person present — symbolizing a business that has gone quiet; bright daylight through a window, clean modern interior, slightly lonely atmosphere without being dark.

**voiceover_text**

I'll be honest — I blocked two hours every Tuesday for content. Script it, film it, edit it, caption it, resize it for five platforms. By 4 PM I'd posted exactly nothing and rescheduled it to Thursday. Every. Single. Week. Turns out the routine wasn't the problem. The production was. Give fenrik Studio your website URL — your first content package is free, no payment needed.

**video concept**

A founder's confident Tuesday content block — shown as a repeating weekly ritual — slowly unravels into the same empty result every time. The twist: the problem was never motivation or discipline; it was production volume. The punchline reframes the entire 'content routine' as a production problem that a website URL quietly solves. Fast-cut vertical short, light and dry humor, bright modern workspace setting.

**video script**

BEAT 1 — SITUATION (0–5s): Open on a bright, tidy home office desk. A calendar notification glows on a blurred laptop screen: 'Tuesday Content Block — 2hrs'. Founder sits down confidently, cracking knuckles. VO: 'I blocked two hours every Tuesday for content.'

BEAT 2 — UNEXPECTED TURN (5–13s): Quick cuts — sticky note with a script, phone propped on books for filming, frustrated face staring at a resize dialog, five platform icons floating above a half-finished caption. Clock jumps from 2 PM to 4 PM. VO: 'Script it. Film it. Edit it. Caption it. Resize it. Five platforms. By 4 PM — posted exactly nothing. Rescheduled to Thursday. Every. Single. Week.'

BEAT 3 — PUNCHLINE (13–19s): Founder leans back, smirks at camera, arms crossed. A single URL typed into a browser — screen blurred, just the gesture visible. VO: 'Turns out the routine wasn't the problem. The production was.'

BEAT 4 — CTA (19–24s): Clean bright end card, warm tone. VO: 'Give fenrik Studio your website URL — your first content package is free, no payment needed.'
